{"id":"820a0538-88cf-409e-88bd-f00ddbf2efc2","identifier":"FRG-176","title":"v2 Phase 2: Preview polish, PDF export, mutation warning, error states","description":"## Context

Phase 1 merged (PR #31). App has textarea → OpenAI gpt-4o-mini → XML → DOMPurify → v-html preview. Phase 2 polishes the output and adds export.

## Requirements

### 1\\. Professional CSS Template (modern.css)

The current `resume-styles.css` needs to match the spec from `mvp-features.md`:

* Font: `Inter, 'DM Sans', system-ui, -apple-system, sans-serif` (not serif)
* Name: 22px, font-weight 700
* Section headers: 13px, font-weight 600, ALL CAPS, letter-spacing 0.05em, border-bottom 1.5px solid
* Body text: 13px, font-weight 400, line-height 1.5
* Contact info: 12px, color #555
* Max width 800px centered, padding 48px 64px
* Role title + dates on same line via flexbox (title left, period right)
* Bullet points properly indented

### 2\\. Mutation Warning

* Always show neutral review note below preview: \"Your content has been formatted but not rewritten. Please review before exporting.\"
* If divergence > 5% (0.05): show amber warning banner ABOVE the Export button: \"⚠ Some content may have been changed during formatting. Please review carefully before exporting.\"
* Warning does NOT block export

### 3\\. PDF Export

* \"Export PDF\" button triggers `window.print()`
* `@media print` CSS: hide header, textarea, buttons, warning — only document prints
* `@page { size: A4; margin: 0.75in; }`
* `page-break-inside: avoid` on sections
* Links print as black text, no underline
* Small note near button: \"Works best in Chrome. In the print dialog, choose 'Save as PDF'.\"

### 4\\. Error States (verify/improve)

* API error → \"Something went wrong. Please try again.\" + Try Again button
* Short input (<50 chars) → inline message, don't call API
* Malformed XML → same as API error, log raw response to console

### 5\\. Input Validation

* Button disabled when textarea empty
* Min 50 chars to submit (show inline message if too short)
* Textarea disabled during generation

   102→const formattedXml = ref('')
   103→const isFormatting = ref(false)

   106→
   107→function handlePrint() {
   108→  window.print()
   109→}
   110→
   111→async function formatDocument() {
   112→  if (!textContent.value.trim() || isFormatting.value) return
   113→  isFormatting.value = true
   114→  formatError.value = ''
   115→  formattedXml.value = ''
   116→  documentType.value = ''
   117→

   119→    const result = await $fetch<{ xml: string, divergence: number, documentType: string }>('/api/format', {
   120→      method: 'POST',
   121→      body: { text: textContent.value },
   122→    })
   123→    formattedXml.value = result.xml
   124→    documentType.value = result.documentType
   125→  }
   126→  catch (err: unknown) {
   127→    const message = (err as { data?: { message?: string } })?.data?.message
   128→    formatError.value = message || 'Something went wrong. Please try again.'
   129→  }
   130→  finally {
   131→    isFormatting.value = false
   132→  }
   133→}

    48→interface OpenAIChatResponse {
    49→  choices: Array<{
    50→    message: {
    51→      content: string
    52→    }
    53→  }>

    55→
    56→function extractTextFromXml(xmlString: string): string {
    57→  const textParts: string[] = []
    58→  const parser = new Parser({
    59→    ontext(text) {
    60→      textParts.push(text)
    61→    },
    62→  }, { decodeEntities: true })
    63→  parser.write(xmlString)
    64→  parser.end()
    65→  return textParts.join(' ')
    66→}
    67→
    68→function detectDocumentType(xmlString: string): string {
    69→  const match = xmlString.match(/<document[^>]+type="([^"]+)"/)
    70→  return match?.[1] ?? 'resume'
    71→}
    72→
    73→function validateXmlStructure(xmlString: string): boolean {
    74→  let valid = true
    75→  let depth = 0
    76→  const parser = new Parser({
    77→    onerror() {
    78→      valid = false
    79→    },
    80→    onopentag() {
    81→      depth++
    82→    },
    83→    onclosetag() {
    84→      depth--
    85→      if (depth < 0) valid = false
    86→    },
    87→  }, { xmlMode: true })
    88→  parser.write(xmlString)
    89→  parser.end()
    90→  return valid && depth === 0
    91→}

     1→/**

     3→ *
     4→ * Provides XML parsing functionality using browser's native DOMParser API.
     5→ * Zero dependencies approach for fast, simple XML parsing (DECISIONS.md Decision 6).

     7→
     8→// TypeScript interfaces matching the XML schema from docs/sample/cover-letter.xml

    10→export interface Address {
    11→  street: string
    12→  city: string
    13→  state: string
    14→  zipCode: string
    15→}

    30→}

    54→  applicant: Applicant

    59→
    60→export interface ValidationResult {
    61→  isValid: boolean
    62→  error?: string
    63→}
    64→
    65→export interface ParseResult {
    66→  success: boolean
    67→  data?: unknown
    68→  error?: string
    69→}
    70→
    71→/**
    72→ * Helper function to safely extract text content from an XML element
    73→ */
    74→function getTextContent(element: Element | null, tagName: string, parentName: string = 'document'): string {
    75→  if (!element) {
    76→    throw new Error(`Missing required element: ${tagName} in ${parentName}`)
    77→  }
    78→  const node = element.querySelector(tagName)
    79→  if (!node) {
    80→    throw new Error(`Missing required element: ${tagName} in ${parentName}`)
    81→  }
    82→  return node.textContent?.trim() || ''
    83→}
    84→
    85→/**
    86→ * Parse address element (reusable for applicant and recipient addresses)
    87→ */
    88→function parseAddress(addressElement: Element | null, context: string): Address {
    89→  if (!addressElement) {
    90→    throw new Error(`Missing address element in ${context}`)
    91→  }
    92→
    93→  return {
    94→    street: getTextContent(addressElement, 'street', `${context} address`),
    95→    city: getTextContent(addressElement, 'city', `${context} address`),
    96→    state: getTextContent(addressElement, 'state', `${context} address`),
    97→    zipCode: getTextContent(addressElement, 'zipCode', `${context} address`),
    98→  }
    99→}
   100→
   101→/**
   102→ * Validate XML for well-formedness and basic schema requirements
   103→ *
   104→ * @param xmlString - XML string to validate
   105→ * @returns ValidationResult with isValid flag and optional error message
   106→ */
   107→export function validateXml(xmlString: string): ValidationResult {
   108→  if (!xmlString || xmlString.trim() === '') {
   109→    return {
   110→      isValid: false,
   111→      error: 'XML input is empty. Please provide valid XML content.',
   112→    }
   113→  }
   114→
   115→  const parser = new DOMParser()
   116→  const xmlDoc = parser.parseFromString(xmlString, 'text/xml')
   117→
   118→  // Check for parser errors
   119→  const parserError = xmlDoc.querySelector('parsererror')
   120→  if (parserError) {
   121→    // Extract meaningful error message from parsererror element
   122→    const errorText = parserError.textContent || 'Unknown XML parsing error'
   123→
   124→    // Provide user-friendly error messages for common issues
   125→    if (errorText.includes('unclosed tag') || errorText.includes('Opening and ending tag mismatch')) {
   126→      return {
   127→        isValid: false,
   128→        error: 'XML has unclosed or mismatched tags. Please check that all opening tags have corresponding closing tags.',
   129→      }
   130→    }
   131→    if (errorText.includes('Unexpected end of file') || errorText.includes('premature end of data')) {
   132→      return {
   133→        isValid: false,
   134→        error: 'XML is incomplete. The document appears to end unexpectedly.',
   135→      }
   136→    }
   137→    if (errorText.includes('invalid character') || errorText.includes('not well-formed')) {
   138→      return {
   139→        isValid: false,
   140→        error: 'XML contains invalid characters or syntax. Please check for special characters that need to be escaped.',
   141→      }
   142→    }
   143→
   144→    return {
   145→      isValid: false,
   146→      error: `XML parsing error: ${errorText}`,
   147→    }
   148→  }
   149→
   150→  // Check for root element
   151→  const root = xmlDoc.documentElement
   152→  if (!root || root.tagName !== 'applicationDocument') {
   153→    return {
   154→      isValid: false,
   155→      error: 'Invalid XML structure. Root element must be <applicationDocument>.',
   156→    }
   157→  }
   158→
   159→  // Check for required top-level elements
   160→  const requiredElements = ['applicant', 'date', 'recipient', 'letter']
   161→  for (const elementName of requiredElements) {
   162→    if (!root.querySelector(elementName)) {
   163→      return {
   164→        isValid: false,
   165→        error: `Missing required element: <${elementName}>. All application documents must include applicant, date, recipient, and letter sections.`,
   166→      }
   167→    }
   168→  }
   169→
   170→  return { isValid: true }
   171→}
   172→
   173→/**
   174→ * Parse XML string into structured data object
   175→ *
   176→ * @param xmlString - XML string to parse
   177→ * @returns ParseResult with success flag, parsed data, or error message
   178→ */
   179→export function parseXml(xmlString: string): ParseResult {
   180→  try {
   181→    // First validate the XML
   182→    const validation = validateXml(xmlString)
   183→    if (!validation.isValid) {
   184→      return {
   185→        success: false,
   186→        error: validation.error,
   187→      }
   188→    }
   189→
   190→    const parser = new DOMParser()
   191→    const xmlDoc = parser.parseFromString(xmlString, 'text/xml')
   192→    const root = xmlDoc.documentElement
   193→
   194→    // Extract formatStyle attribute (optional)
   195→    const formatStyle = root.getAttribute('formatStyle') || undefined
   196→
   197→    // Parse applicant section
   198→    const applicantElement = root.querySelector('applicant')
   199→    if (!applicantElement) {
   200→      throw new Error('Missing required element: applicant')
   201→    }
   202→
   203→    const applicant: Applicant = {
   204→      name: getTextContent(applicantElement, 'name', 'applicant'),
   205→      address: parseAddress(applicantElement.querySelector('address'), 'applicant'),
   206→      contactInformation: {
   207→        phone: getTextContent(applicantElement, 'contactInformation phone', 'applicant'),
   208→        email: getTextContent(applicantElement, 'contactInformation email', 'applicant'),
   209→      },
   210→    }
   211→
   212→    // Parse date
   213→    const date = getTextContent(root, 'date')
   214→
   215→    // Parse recipient section
   216→    const recipientElement = root.querySelector('recipient')
   217→    if (!recipientElement) {
   218→      throw new Error('Missing required element: recipient')
   219→    }
   220→
   221→    const recipient: Recipient = {
   222→      position: getTextContent(recipientElement, 'position', 'recipient'),
   223→      company: getTextContent(recipientElement, 'company', 'recipient'),
   224→      address: parseAddress(recipientElement.querySelector('address'), 'recipient'),
   225→    }
   226→
   227→    // Parse letter section
   228→    const letterElement = root.querySelector('letter')
   229→    if (!letterElement) {
   230→      throw new Error('Missing required element: letter')
   231→    }
   232→
   233→    // Parse experiences
   234→    const experienceElements = letterElement.querySelectorAll('experienceSection experience')
   235→    const experiences: Experience[] = Array.from(experienceElements).map((expElement) => {
   236→      const employer = expElement.querySelector('employer')?.textContent?.trim() || ''
   237→      const achievementElements = expElement.querySelectorAll('achievements achievement')
   238→      const achievements: Achievement[] = Array.from(achievementElements).map(ach => ({
   239→        text: ach.textContent?.trim() || '',
   240→      }))
   241→
   242→      return {
   243→        employer,
   244→        achievements,
   245→      }
   246→    })
   247→
   248→    const letter: Letter = {
   249→      salutation: getTextContent(letterElement, 'salutation', 'letter'),
   250→      introduction: getTextContent(letterElement, 'introduction', 'letter'),
   251→      experienceSection: experiences,
   252→      motivation: getTextContent(letterElement, 'motivation', 'letter'),
   253→      closing: getTextContent(letterElement, 'closing', 'letter'),
   254→      signature: getTextContent(letterElement, 'signature', 'letter'),
   255→    }
   256→
   257→    const parsedData: ParsedData = {
   258→      formatStyle,
   259→      applicant,
   260→      date,
   261→      recipient,
   262→      letter,
   263→    }
   264→
   265→    return {
   266→      success: true,
   267→      data: parsedData,
   268→    }
   269→  }
   270→  catch (error) {
   271→    const errorMessage = error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Unknown error occurred during parsing'
   272→    return {
   273→      success: false,
   274→      error: `Failed to parse XML: ${errorMessage}`,
   275→    }
   276→  }
   277→}
   278→
   279→/**
   280→ * Composable function to use XML parser in Vue components
   281→ */
   282→export function useXmlParser() {
   283→  return {
   284→    parseXml,
   285→    validateXml,
   286→  }
   287→}

    12→    />
    13→
    14→    <!-- Document Preview — content is DOMPurify-sanitized before assignment to sanitizedHtml -->
    15→    <!-- eslint-disable vue/no-v-html -->
    16→    <div
    17→      v-else-if="sanitizedHtml"
    18→      class="preview-container document-render"
    19→      :style="containerStyle"
    20→      v-html="sanitizedHtml"
    21→    />
    22→    <!-- eslint-enable vue/no-v-html -->
    23→
    24→    <!-- Placeholder State -->

    26→      <p>Preparing preview…</p>

    29→</template>
    30→
    31→<script setup lang="ts">
    32→import { ref, computed, watch } from 'vue'
    33→import './resume-styles.css'
    34→
    35→defineOptions({ name: 'PreviewPanel' })
    36→
    37→interface Props {
    38→  xmlContent: string
    39→  zoom?: number
    40→}
    41→
    42→const props = withDefaults(defineProps<Props>(), { zoom: 1 })
    43→
    44→const sanitizedHtml = ref<string>('')
    45→const error = ref<string | undefined>(undefined)
    46→
    47→const containerStyle = computed(() => ({
    48→  transform: `scale(${props.zoom})`,
    49→  transformOrigin: 'top left',
    50→}))
    51→
    52→const ALLOWED_TAGS = [
    53→  'document', 'header', 'name', 'contact', 'email', 'phone', 'location',
    54→  'linkedin', 'website', 'summary', 'experience', 'role', 'title', 'company',
    55→  'period', 'bullets', 'bullet', 'education', 'degree', 'school', 'year',
    56→  'note', 'skills', 'certifications', 'projects', 'volunteer',
    57→  // Standard HTML tags DOMPurify allows anyway — kept for section labels
    58→  'section', 'h2', 'p', 'ul', 'li', 'a', 'br', 'strong', 'em',
    59→]
    60→
    61→const ALLOWED_ATTR = ['type', 'href']
    62→
    63→async function updatePreview() {
    64→  error.value = undefined
    65→  sanitizedHtml.value = ''
    66→
    67→  if (!props.xmlContent) return
    68→
    69→  try {
    70→    // DOMPurify is browser-only — import lazily to avoid SSR issues
    71→    const DOMPurify = (await import('dompurify')).default
    72→    const clean = DOMPurify.sanitize(props.xmlContent, {
    73→      ADD_TAGS: ALLOWED_TAGS,
    74→      ADD_ATTR: ALLOWED_ATTR,
    75→      FORCE_BODY: false,
    76→    })
    77→    sanitizedHtml.value = clean
    78→  }
    79→  catch (err) {
    80→    error.value = err instanceof Error ? err.message : 'Could not render document'
    81→  }
    82→}
    83→
    84→watch(() => props.xmlContent, updatePreview, { immediate: true })
    85→</script>
    86→
    87→<style scoped>
    88→.preview-panel {

    41→        {{ data.recipient.address.street }}<br>

    43→      </address>
    44→    </div>
    45→
    46→    <!-- Letter Content -->
    47→    <main v-if="data.letter" class="letter">
    48→      <!-- Salutation -->
    49→      <p v-if="data.letter.salutation" class="salutation">
    50→        {{ data.letter.salutation }}
    51→      </p>
    52→
    53→      <!-- Introduction -->
    54→      <p v-if="data.letter.introduction" class="introduction">
    55→        {{ data.letter.introduction }}
    56→      </p>
    57→
    58→      <!-- Experience Section -->
    59→      <div v-if="data.letter.experienceSection && data.letter.experienceSection.length > 0" class="experience-section">
    60→        <div
    61→          v-for="(experience, expIndex) in data.letter.experienceSection"
    62→          :key="expIndex"
    63→          class="experience"
    64→        >
    65→          <p v-if="experience.employer" class="experience-employer">
    66→            <strong>{{ experience.employer }}</strong>
    67→          </p>
    68→          <ul v-if="experience.achievements && experience.achievements.length > 0" class="achievements">
    69→            <li
    70→              v-for="(achievement, achIndex) in experience.achievements"
    71→              :key="achIndex"
    72→              class="achievement"
    73→            >
    74→              {{ achievement.text }}
    75→            </li>
    76→          </ul>
    77→        </div>
    78→      </div>
    79→
    80→      <!-- Motivation -->
    81→      <p v-if="data.letter.motivation" class="motivation">
    82→        {{ data.letter.motivation }}
    83→      </p>
    84→
    85→      <!-- Closing -->
    86→      <p v-if="data.letter.closing" class="closing">
    87→        {{ data.letter.closing }}
    88→      </p>
    89→
    90→      <!-- Signature -->
    91→      <p v-if="data.letter.signature" class="signature">
    92→        {{ data.letter.signature }}
    93→      </p>
    94→    </main>
    95→  </article>
    96→</template>
    97→
    98→<script setup lang="ts">
    99→import type { ParsedData } from '~/composables/useXmlParser'
   100→import './styles.css'
   101→
   102→/**
   103→ * Modern Template Component
   104→ *
   105→ * Renders a cover letter in a modern, professional style.
   106→ * Uses only standard HTML elements and scoped CSS (no @nuxt/ui components).
   107→ * This ensures the template can be exported as standalone HTML.
   108→ *
   109→ * CSS Import Strategy:
   110→ * - CSS is imported as a module in the script section
   111→ * - This ensures reliable loading across all deployment platforms (including Vercel)
   112→ * - The <style scoped> block below adds component-specific scoping
   113→ * - Maintains CSS separation: styles.css remains a separate, maintainable file
   114→ */
   115→
   116→interface Props {
   117→  data: ParsedData
   118→}
   119→
   120→defineProps<Props>()
   121→</script>
   122→
   123→<style scoped>
   124→/**
   125→ * Modern Template Styles
   126→ *
   127→ * The actual CSS is imported as a module in the <script> section above.
   128→ * This style block is kept to apply Vue's scoped CSS mechanism.
   129→ *
   130→ * Why this approach:
   131→ * - Both @import and src attribute had issues in production/Vercel
   132→ * - Script import ensures CSS is bundled and loaded correctly
   133→ * - Empty scoped block ensures Vue adds scoping attributes to all elements
   134→ * - Maintains architecture: CSS file separate, scoping applied
   135→ */
   136→</style>
   137→

     1→# MVP Development Plan
     2→
     3→**Project**: ohmydoc-v2 - XML-to-HTML Real-Time Transformer
     4→**Date**: 2025-10-11
     5→**Version**: 1.0
     6→**Status**: Approved
     7→
     8→## Overview
     9→
    10→This document outlines the agile MVP breakdown for developing the XML-to-HTML transformer application. Each MVP delivers a working, testable, and usable component that builds progressively toward the complete application.
    11→
    12→## Development Principles
    13→
    14→1. **Agile**: Each MVP is independently usable and testable
    15→2. **Progressive**: Later MVPs build on earlier ones using reusable components
    16→3. **Demo-Driven**: Debug pages at `/debug/*` demonstrate component capabilities
    17→4. **Functionality First**: Focus on working features before optimization
    18→5. **Component Reusability**: Components built in demo pages are reused in main app
    19→
    20→## MVP Breakdown
    21→
    22→---
    23→
    24→### MVP 1: Basic App Shell
    25→
    26→**Goal**: Foundation with header and routing ready
    27→
    28→**What to Build**:
    29→- Basic app layout structure (app.vue or pages structure)
    30→- `components/AppHeader.vue` using @nuxt/ui components (UContainer, title text)
    31→- Initially: just app title, empty action slots for future buttons
    32→- Verify routing works (can navigate to `/debug/parser`)
    33→
    34→**Deliverable**:
    35→- App loads with header displaying app title
    36→- Navigation to `/debug/*` pages works
    37→- @nuxt/ui styling applied
    38→
    39→**Reusable Components**:

    41→
    42→**Acceptance Criteria**:

    45→- [ ] Can navigate to `/debug/parser` (even if page is empty)
    46→- [ ] @nuxt/ui components render correctly
    47→
    48→---
    49→
    50→### MVP 2: XML Parser with Interactive Demo

    56→  - `ParsedData` interface matching XML schema
    57→  - `parseXml(xmlString)` function
    58→  - `validateXml(xmlString)` function
    59→- Create page: `pages/debug/parser.vue`

    61→  - Button to trigger parse (use @nuxt/ui `UButton`)
    62→  - Display parsed JSON output (formatted)

    65→

    71→
    72→**Reusable Components**:
    73→- `composables/useXmlParser.ts` - used by all preview/rendering MVPs
    74→

  validate with htmlparser2, calculate divergence, return documentType

  sanitization + v-html render for new <document> XML schema

  elements (document, header, name, contact, experience, role, etc.)
- package.json: add dompurify + @types/dompurify

     1→# Product Requirements Document: XML-to-HTML Real-Time Transformer
     2→
     3→## 1. Overview
     4→
     5→### 1.1 Product Vision
     6→A modern, browser-based real-time transformer application that allows users to edit structured XML documents and see instant HTML preview rendering. The application focuses on document formatting (e.g., cover letters, resumes) with a clean, intuitive interface. **This is a Proof of Concept (PoC) version** focusing on core functionality with code-level template extensibility.
     7→
     8→### 1.2 Target Users
     9→- Content creators and writers
    10→- HR professionals and recruiters
    11→- Document designers
    12→- Developers working with XML/HTML transformations
    13→
    14→### 1.3 Tech Stack
    15→- **Framework**: Nuxt.js (latest version via `npm create nuxt@latest`)
    16→- **Language**: TypeScript
    17→- **UI Components**: @nuxt/ui for application chrome (buttons, inputs, modals, alerts)
    18→- **Styling**: Vue Scoped CSS for document templates (exportable content)
    19→- **XML Parsing**: DOMParser (native browser API)
    20→- **Code Editor**: Monaco Editor via `nuxt-monaco-editor`
    21→
    22→---
    23→
    24→## 2. Functional Requirements
    25→
    26→### 2.1 Core Features
    27→
    28→#### 2.1.1 Dual-Panel Layout
    29→- **Left Panel**: XML Editor
    30→  - Syntax highlighting for XML
    31→  - Line numbers
    32→  - Auto-indentation
    33→  - Real-time validation
    34→  - Resizable panel width
    35→
    36→- **Right Panel**: HTML Preview
    37→  - Live rendering of transformed HTML using Vue templates
    38→  - Styled according to the active template's CSS
    39→  - Scrollable content area
    40→  - Responsive layout
    41→
    42→#### 2.1.2 Real-Time Transformation
    43→- **Initial State**: Application loads with sample XML (`public/samples/cover-letter.xml`) pre-populated in editor on first load
    44→- **Instant Updates**: Changes in XML editor trigger immediate preview updates
    45→- **Debouncing**: Implement 300ms debounce to optimize performance
    46→- **Error Handling**: Display friendly error messages for invalid XML
    47→- **Syntax Validation**: Highlight XML syntax errors in the editor
    48→
    49→#### 2.1.3 XML Schema Support
    50→Based on `docs/sample/cover-letter.xml`, the application should support the following XML structure:
    51→
    52→```xml
    53→<applicationDocument>
    54→  <applicant>
    55→    <name>...</name>
    56→    <address>
    57→      <street>...</street>
    58→      <city>...</city>
    59→      <state>...</state>
    60→      <zipCode>...</zipCode>
    61→    </address>
    62→    <contactInformation>
    63→      <phone>...</phone>
    64→      <email>...</email>
    65→    </contactInformation>
    66→  </applicant>
    67→  <date>...</date>
    68→  <recipient>
    69→    <position>...</position>
    70→    <company>...</company>
    71→    <address>...</address>
    72→  </recipient>
    73→  <letter>
    74→    <salutation>...</salutation>
    75→    <introduction>...</introduction>
    76→    <experienceSection>
    77→      <experience>
    78→        <employer>...</employer>
    79→        <achievements>
    80→          <achievement>...</achievement>
    81→        </achievements>
    82→      </experience>
    83→    </experienceSection>
    84→    <motivation>...</motivation>
    85→    <closing>...</closing>
    86→    <signature>...</signature>
    87→  </letter>
    88→</applicationDocument>
    89→```
    90→
    91→**Note**: The XML structure is standardized and does NOT include a `formatStyle` attribute. Template selection is handled at the code level only.
    92→
    93→#### 2.1.4 Template-Based Rendering
    94→The application uses **Vue Single File Components (SFCs)** as templates:
    95→
    96→- Each template is a `.vue` file with its own HTML structure and scoped CSS
    97→- Templates render the same XML data but with completely different HTML structures
    98→- CSS is template-specific and swaps out entirely when templates change
    99→- **PoC Scope**: Templates are swapped by changing a configuration constant in code (no UI control)
   100→

<system-reminder>
Whenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.
</system-reminder>

SUCCESS 
     1→# Architectural Decisions & Key Concepts
     2→
     3→**Project**: ohmydoc-v2
     4→**Date**: 2025-10-11
     5→**Version**: 1.0
     6→
     7→## Overview
     8→
     9→This document captures the key architectural decisions, rationale, and concepts that shaped the MVP plan for the XML-to-HTML transformer application. Future developers and AI agents should reference this to understand the "why" behind the structure.
    10→
    11→---
    12→
    13→## Decision 1: Agile MVP Approach
    14→
    15→### Decision
    16→Break down development into 12 progressive MVPs, each delivering a working, testable component.
    17→
    18→### Rationale
    19→- **Agile Principle**: Each MVP is independently usable, not just a partial feature
    20→- **Risk Mitigation**: Catch issues early with incremental testing
    21→- **Flexibility**: Can adjust priorities or pivot based on learnings from each MVP
    22→- **Demonstrable Progress**: Stakeholders see working features at each stage
    23→- **AI Agent Friendly**: Each MVP has clear, bounded scope for autonomous execution
    24→
    25→### Alternatives Considered
    26→- **Waterfall**: Build all components, then integrate → Rejected: High risk of integration issues
    27→- **Feature-based**: Group by features (editor, preview, export) → Rejected: Less granular, harder to test incrementally
    28→
    29→### Impact
    30→- Development follows MVP-PLAN.md sequence (MVP 1 → MVP 12)
    31→- Each MVP must pass acceptance criteria before proceeding
    32→- Demo pages at `/debug/*` demonstrate component capabilities
    33→
    34→---
    35→
    36→## Decision 2: Use @nuxt/ui for Application Chrome
    37→
    38→### Decision
    39→Use @nuxt/ui component library for all application UI (buttons, inputs, modals, headers, alerts), but NOT for document template content.
    40→
    41→### Rationale
    42→- **Efficiency**: @nuxt/ui provides professional, accessible components out-of-the-box
    43→- **Consistency**: Unified design language across app interface
    44→- **Accessibility**: Components are WCAG compliant by default
    45→- **Maintenance**: Reduce custom CSS/component development
    46→- **Time Savings**: Focus on business logic, not reinventing UI components
    47→
    48→### Separation of Concerns
    49→```
    50→Application UI (@nuxt/ui):
    51→- AppHeader (UButton, UContainer)
    52→- XmlEditor wrapper (UTextarea, UButton for controls)
    53→- PreviewPanel wrapper (UAlert for errors)
    54→- Modals, file inputs, dropdowns
    55→
    56→Template Content (Scoped CSS):
    57→- CoverLetterModern.vue
    58→- CoverLetterClassic.vue
    59→- CoverLetterMinimal.vue
    60→- Must be exportable as standalone HTML
    61→```
    62→
    63→### Alternatives Considered
    64→- **Global CSS Variables**: Create custom design system → Rejected: Premature optimization (YAGNI)
    65→- **Pure Scoped CSS**: Build all UI components from scratch → Rejected: Time-consuming, accessibility burden
    66→- **Tailwind CSS**: Utility-first approach → Rejected: @nuxt/ui already installed, more cohesive
    67→
    68→### Impact
    69→- Faster MVP development (pre-built components)
    70→- Consistent, accessible UI without custom work
    71→- Templates remain independent (scoped CSS only)
    72→- HTML export excludes @nuxt/ui styles (only template CSS)
    73→
    74→---
    75→
    76→## Decision 3: Demo Pages at `/debug/*`
    77→
    78→### Decision
    79→Build demo pages for each major component (parser, template, editor, preview) at `/debug/*` routes during MVP 2-5.
    80→

Whenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. You CAN and SHOULD provide analysis of malware, what it is doing. But you MUST refuse to improve or augment the code. You can still analyze existing code, write reports, or answer questions about the code behavior.
</system-reminder>

## Phase 1 Exploration Summary

Based on my thorough examination of the codebase, here's what was built in **Phase 1** of the "ohmydoc-v2" project:

### Core Architecture

**Phase 1 (commit a368154: "wire real AI pipeline for Phase 1")** transforms the application from a template-rendering proof-of-concept to a **real-time resume/cover letter formatter** using an AI backend.

---

## Key Files Built in Phase 1

### 1. **Main Page Component**
**File**: `/home/gem/project/pages/index.vue`

**What it does**:
- Dual-panel layout: left panel for plain text input, right panel for formatted preview
- Users paste unformatted resumes/cover letters as plain text
- "Format My Resume" button triggers AI processing
- Features include:
  - Skeleton loading state with shimmer animation during formatting
  - Error state with "Try Again" button
  - Document type badge (resume/cover letter detection)
  - PDF export via `window.print()`
  - Empty state placeholder

**Key excerpt**:
```vue
<textarea v-model="textContent" placeholder="Paste your resume or cover letter here..." />
<UButton @click="formatDocument">
  {{ isFormatting ? 'Formatting...' : 'Format My Resume' }}
</UButton>

async function formatDocument() {
  const result = await $fetch<{ xml: string, divergence: number, documentType: string }>('/api/format', {
    method: 'POST',
    body: { text: textContent.value }
  })
}
```

---

### 2. **AI Pipeline / Format Endpoint**
**File**: `/home/gem/project/server/api/format.post.ts`

**What it does**:
- Server-side Nuxt API route that calls OpenAI's GPT-4o-mini model
- Converts plain text resumes/cover letters into structured XML
- Validates generated XML structure using htmlparser2
- Calculates "divergence" metric (how much text content changed)
- Detects document type (resume vs cover letter)

**Key excerpt**:
```typescript
// System prompt instructs AI to output XML schema:
const SYSTEM_PROMPT = `You are a professional document formatter. Convert plain-text resumes and cover letters into structured XML.

For resumes use this schema:
<document type="resume">
  <header>
    <name>Full Name</name>
    <contact>...</contact>
  </header>
  <summary>...</summary>
  <experience>
    <role>
      <title>...</title>
      <company>...</company>
      <period>...</period>
      <bullets>
        <bullet>...</bullet>
      </bullets>
    </role>
  </experience>
  <education>...</education>
  <skills>...</skills>
  ...
</document>`

// Calls OpenAI API with gpt-4o-mini model
const response = await $fetch('https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions', {
  body: {
    model: 'gpt-4o-mini',
    messages: [
      { role: 'system', content: SYSTEM_PROMPT },
      { role: 'user', content: body.text }
    ],
    temperature: 0.3,
    max_tokens: 4000
  }
})

// Validates XML structure and returns metadata
return { xml, divergence, documentType }
```

---

### 3. **Resume Styling System**
**File**: `/home/gem/project/components/resume-styles.css`

**What it does**:
- Defines block-level styling for custom AI-generated XML elements
- Styles custom elements: `<document>`, `<header>`, `<name>`, `<contact>`, `<experience>`, `<role>`, `<company>`, `<period>`, `<bullets>`, `<bullet>`, `<education>`, `<degree>`, `<school>`, `<year>`, `<skills>`, `<certifications>`, `<projects>`, `<volunteer>`
- Uses design system variables: `--ink: #111`, `--muted: #555`, `--accent: #0f6fec`
- Includes print-optimized styles (`@media print`)

**Key excerpt**:

/* ── Custom element resets ── */
document, header, name, contact, email, phone, location,
experience, role, title, company, period, bullets, bullet,
education, degree, school, year, skills, certifications,
projects, volunteer {

### 4. **Preview Panel Component (Updated)**
**File**: `/home/gem/project/components/PreviewPanel.vue`

**Changes in Phase 1**:
- Replaced old DOMParser flow with **DOMPurify sanitization**
- Now handles new custom XML elements from AI pipeline
- Uses `v-html` for rendering sanitized content
- Imports new `resume-styles.css` for custom element styling

**Key excerpt**:
```vue
const ALLOWED_TAGS = [
  'document', 'header', 'name', 'contact', 'email', 'phone', 'location',
  'linkedin', 'website', 'summary', 'experience', 'role', 'title', 'company',
  'period', 'bullets', 'bullet', 'education', 'degree', 'school', 'year',
  'note', 'skills', 'certifications', 'projects', 'volunteer',
  'section', 'h2', 'p', 'ul', 'li', 'a', 'br', 'strong', 'em',
]

async function updatePreview() {
  const DOMPurify = (await import('dompurify')).default
  const clean = DOMPurify.sanitize(props.xmlContent, {
    ADD_TAGS: ALLOWED_TAGS,
    ADD_ATTR: ['type', 'href'],
    FORCE_BODY: false,
  })
  sanitizedHtml.value = clean
}
```

## Data Flow in Phase 1

```
User Input (Plain Text)
    ↓
POST /api/format
    ↓
OpenAI API (gpt-4o-mini)
    ↓
AI returns custom XML schema:
<document type="resume|cover-letter">
  <header><name>...<contact>...</header>
  <experience>
    <role>
      <title>...<company>...<period>...
      <bullets><bullet>...</bullet></bullets>
    </role>
  </experience>
  ...
</document>
    ↓
Server validates with htmlparser2
    ↓
Returns: { xml, divergence, documentType }
    ↓
PreviewPanel receives XML
    ↓
DOMPurify sanitizes custom elements
    ↓
Render with resume-styles.css
    ↓
HTML preview in right panel + PDF export button
```

✅ **Professional Styling**: resume-styles.css handles block-level layout

✅ **Error Handling**: User-friendly error messages with retry capability
✅ **PDF Export**: Via `window.print()` (print-optimized styles)

## Architecture Notes

Phase 1 represents a **significant shift** from the original MVP plan:
- **Original**: Manual XML editing → Parser → Template rendering
- **Phase 1**: Plain text input → AI formatting → XML generation → Template rendering

This is a **"v2"** feature that leverages AI to eliminate manual XML editing, making the app accessible to non-technical users.

The application now follows this stack:
- **Frontend**: Nuxt 4 + Vue 3 + @nuxt/ui (application chrome) + scoped CSS (templates)
- **Backend**: Nitro API route calling OpenAI API
- **Validation**: htmlparser2 (server) + DOMPurify (client)
- **Styling**: Custom XML element styles + design system variables

     4→
     5→For resumes use this schema:
     6→<document type="resume">
     7→  <header>
     8→    <name>Full Name</name>

    33→  </education>
    34→  <skills>Skill 1, Skill 2, Skill 3</skills>
    35→  <certifications>Cert 1, Cert 2</certifications>
    36→  <projects>Project descriptions</projects>
    37→  <volunteer>Volunteer experience</volunteer>
    38→</document>
    39→
    40→For cover letters use type="cover-letter" and adapt content into letter sections using summary (opening), experience (body paragraphs), and closing elements.
    41→
    42→Rules:
    43→- Preserve ALL information from the source text
    44→- Omit empty optional tags
    45→- Output ONLY valid XML — no markdown fences, no explanation
    46→- Detect whether the input is a resume or cover letter and set the type attribute accordingly`
    47→
    48→interface OpenAIChatResponse {
    49→  choices: Array<{
    50→    message: {
    51→      content: string
    52→    }
    53→  }>
    54→}
    55→
    56→function extractTextFromXml(xmlString: string): string {
    57→  const textParts: string[] = []
    58→  const parser = new Parser({
    59→    ontext(text) {
    60→      textParts.push(text)
    61→    },
    62→  }, { decodeEntities: true })
    63→  parser.write(xmlString)
    64→  parser.end()
    65→  return textParts.join(' ')
    66→}
    67→
    68→function detectDocumentType(xmlString: string): string {
    69→  const match = xmlString.match(/<document[^>]+type="([^"]+)"/)
    70→  return match?.[1] ?? 'resume'
    71→}
    72→
    73→function validateXmlStructure(xmlString: string): boolean {
    74→  let valid = true
    75→  let depth = 0
    76→  const parser = new Parser({
    77→    onerror() {
    78→      valid = false
    79→    },
    80→    onopentag() {
    81→      depth++
    82→    },
    83→    onclosetag() {
    84→      depth--
    85→      if (depth < 0) valid = false
    86→    },
    87→  }, { xmlMode: true })
    88→  parser.write(xmlString)
    89→  parser.end()
    90→  return valid && depth === 0
    91→}
    92→
    93→export default defineEventHandler(async (event) => {
    94→  const body = await readBody(event)
    95→
    96→  if (!body.text || body.text.length < 50) {
    97→    throw createError({ statusCode: 400, message: 'Paste more content to format.' })
    98→  }
    99→
   100→  const config = useRuntimeConfig()
   101→
   102→  if (!config.openaiApiKey) {
   103→    throw createError({ statusCode: 500, message: 'OpenAI API key is not configured.' })
   104→  }
   105→
   106→  const inputLen = body.text.length
   107→
   108→  const response = await $fetch<OpenAIChatResponse>('https://api.openai.com/v1/chat/completions', {
   109→    method: 'POST',
   110→    headers: {
   111→      'Authorization': `Bearer ${config.openaiApiKey}`,
   112→      'Content-Type': 'application/json',
   113→    },
   114→    body: {
   115→      model: 'gpt-4o-mini',
   116→      messages: [
   117→        { role: 'system', content: SYSTEM_PROMPT },
   118→        { role: 'user', content: body.text },
   119→      ],
   120→      temperature: 0.3,
   121→      max_tokens: 4000,
   122→    },
   123→  })
   124→
   125→  const raw = response.choices[0]?.message?.content ?? ''
   126→
   127→  // Strip markdown fences if present
   128→  const xml = raw
   129→    .replace(/^```(?:xml)?
?/m, '')
   130→    .replace(/
?```$/m, '')
   131→    .trim()
   132→
   133→  if (!validateXmlStructure(xml)) {
   134→    throw createError({ statusCode: 502, message: 'AI returned malformed XML. Please try again.' })
   135→  }
   136→
   137→  const xmlText = extractTextFromXml(xml)
   138→  const xmlTextLen = xmlText.length
   139→  const divergence = Math.abs(inputLen - xmlTextLen) / inputLen
   140→
   141→  const documentType = detectDocumentType(xml)
   142→
   143→  return { xml, divergence, documentType }
   144→})

**`components/resume-styles.css`** — full rewrite to modern.css spec:
- Font: `Inter, 'DM Sans', system-ui, -apple-system, sans-serif` (was serif)
- Name: 22px / font-weight 700
- Section headers: 13px / 600 / ALL CAPS / letter-spacing 0.05em / 1.5px solid border-bottom
- Body: 13px / 400 / line-height 1.5; contact 12px / #555
- Layout: max-width 800px, padding 48px 64px
- Flexbox role row: title left, period right via `margin-left: auto`
- `@page { size: A4; margin: 0.75in }` + `page-break-inside: avoid` on sections
- Print links: black text, no underline

**`pages/index.vue`** — UI + validation additions:
- Neutral review note always visible below preview
- Amber divergence warning (> 5%) shown above Export button
- Client-side 50-char minimum with inline validation message (no API call)
- `textarea` disabled during generation
- Export PDF button disabled until document is formatted
- \"Works best in Chrome. In the print dialog, choose 'Save as PDF'.\" hint
- `.no-print` class strategy — hides all UI chrome on print; only document renders
- Raw AI response logged to console when malformed XML returned

### Decisions
- Used `.no-print` CSS class instead of per-element `@media print { display: none }` to keep print rules centralized and easy to audit
- Divergence warning is placed in the header export area (above the Export button) per spec — this keeps it visible without cluttering the preview

{"id":"820a0538-88cf-409e-88bd-f00ddbf2efc2","identifier":"FRG-176","title":"v2 Phase 2: Preview polish, PDF export, mutation warning, error states","description":"## Context

Phase 1 merged (PR #31). App has textarea → OpenAI gpt-4o-mini → XML → DOMPurify → v-html preview. Phase 2 polishes the output and adds export.

## Requirements

### 1\\. Professional CSS Template (modern.css)

The current `resume-styles.css` needs to match the spec from `mvp-features.md`:

* Font: `Inter, 'DM Sans', system-ui, -apple-system, sans-serif` (not serif)
* Name: 22px, font-weight 700
* Section headers: 13px, font-weight 600, ALL CAPS, letter-spacing 0.05em, border-bottom 1.5px solid
* Body text: 13px, font-weight 400, line-height 1.5
* Contact info: 12px, color #555
* Max width 800px centered, padding 48px 64px
* Role title + dates on same line via flexbox (title left, period right)
* Bullet points properly indented

### 2\\. Mutation Warning

* Always show neutral review note below preview: \"Your content has been formatted but not rewritten. Please review before exporting.\"
* If divergence > 5% (0.05): show amber warning banner ABOVE the Export button: \"⚠ Some content may have been changed during formatting. Please review carefully before exporting.\"
* Warning does NOT block export

### 3\\. PDF Export

* \"Export PDF\" button triggers `window.print()`
* `@media print` CSS: hide header, textarea, buttons, warning — only document prints
* `@page { size: A4; margin: 0.75in; }`
* `page-break-inside: avoid` on sections
* Links print as black text, no underline
* Small note near button: \"Works best in Chrome. In the print dialog, choose 'Save as PDF'.\"

### 4\\. Error States (verify/improve)

* API error → \"Something went wrong. Please try again.\" + Try Again button
* Short input (<50 chars) → inline message, don't call API
* Malformed XML → same as API error, log raw response to console

### 5\\. Input Validation

* Button disabled when textarea empty
* Min 50 chars to submit (show inline message if too short)
* Textarea disabled during generation
